Watch CNBC's full interview with White House National Economic Council Director Kevin Hassett

CNBC Television(3.4M)·10:23·12.5K views·2026-06-22
Kevin HassettDirector, White House National Economic Council Alan GreenspanFormer Chairman, Federal Reserve
TL;DRNEC Director Kevin Hassett details the White House’s strategy to lower the national debt through federal workforce cuts and pro-growth tax policies, while highlighting a highly profitable AI boom and successful diplomatic efforts easing global oil markets.
Pioneering...

TL;DR

NEC Director Kevin Hassett details the White House’s strategy to lower the national debt through federal workforce cuts and pro-growth tax policies, while highlighting a highly profitable AI boom and successful diplomatic efforts easing global oil markets.

The Legacy and Innovations of Alan Greenspan

  • Pioneering Technology Adoption: Former Federal Reserve Chairman Alan Greenspan famously allowed the economy to run hot in the late 1990s, anticipating the massive productivity boom of the internet era before it was reflected in official data.
  • The "Order Survey" Method: Long before official government statistics were published, Greenspan had his team directly call CEOs of major corporations (such as GE) to track real-time business orders and technological integration.
  • Monthly Advisory Meetings: During the first Trump administration, Hassett met monthly with Greenspan to discuss policy, noting that Greenspan’s economic mind remained sharp up until his passing.

AI Revolution vs. the Dot-Com Boom

  • Immediate Profitability: Unlike the speculative dot-com bubble of the late 1990s, today's artificial intelligence sector is characterized by immediate, immense profitability.
      • "Printing Money": Both AI providers and the enterprises integrating AI tools are experiencing substantial, tangible profit growth.
  • Unprecedented Economic Scale: Tech leaders like Marc Andreessen and Eric Schmidt view the economic potential of the AI revolution as significantly larger than the initial internet boom.

Federal Debt and Fiscal Policy Strategy

  • Targeting Debt-to-GDP: Lowering the deficit- and debt-to-GDP ratio remains a primary anchor point for President Trump and Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent.
  • Federal Workforce Reductions: The administration has permanently eliminated approximately 300,000 federal jobs, creating structural, long-term budget savings that challenge CBO baseline forecasts.
  • Capital Spending Surge: Tax policies—such as temporary factory expensing and permanent equipment write-offs—have driven a historic surge in capital spending, including a month pointing to a 40% annualized growth rate for non-defense capital goods (excluding aircraft).

Easing Oil Markets and Middle East Diplomacy

  • Price Outlook: Energy futures markets point to oil prices dropping into the $70s as supply concerns ease.
  • Diplomatic Progress in Switzerland: Vice President JD Vance has reported major progress in negotiations with Iran.
      • Nuclear Inspections: Iran has agreed to allow UN inspectors to access its nuclear facilities.
      • Strait of Hormuz Reopened: Major oil tankers are navigating the strait once again, restoring oil transport volumes to near pre-war levels.

Monetary Policy and Federal Reserve Reform

  • Restructuring the Fed: New Fed Chairman Kevin Warsh is actively reorganizing Fed procedures and reviewing legacy models to ensure the central bank avoids past policy delays that led to 9% inflation.
  • Targeting Price Stability: With inflation remaining above the Fed's 2% target for roughly 63 months, the Fed’s immediate focus remains firmly on price stability, supported by a highly resilient labor market.

Notable Quotes

"He was just an absolutely brilliant mind who saw the computer revolution happening before anyone else did... That judgment created an enormous amount of wealth and prosperity for our country." — Kevin Hassett (on Alan Greenspan)
"The thing that's really different about this time is that these AI companies are printing money and the firms that hire them to improve how they operate they're printing money... You don't have to just have an imagination to value these things." — Kevin Hassett
"We've reduced federal employment by about 300,000 workers now. That's a savings—budget savings—that's going to be there forever." — Kevin Hassett

Inside Economics #280 - Breaking in a New Chair

Moody's(10.0K)·51:43·31 views·2026-06-22
Claudia SahmChief Economist, New Century Advisors Kevin WarshChair, Federal Reserve
TL;DRThe Federal Open Market Committee (FOMC) unanimously voted 12–0 to keep interest rates steady at 3.5% to 3.75% during Kevin Warsh's first meeting as Fed Chair, but the panel expressed strong concerns over Warsh's shift toward a highly minimalist,…
less transparent...

TL;DR

The Federal Open Market Committee (FOMC) unanimously voted 12–0 to keep interest rates steady at 3.5% to 3.75% during Kevin Warsh's first meeting as Fed Chair, but the panel expressed strong concerns over Warsh's shift toward a highly minimalist, less transparent communication style and his proposed structural reforms.

***

FOMC Rate Decision and Shifting Policy Bias

  • The Policy Hold: The FOMC voted 12–0 to keep the federal funds rate unchanged at 3.5% to 3.75%.
      • Inflation Pressures: Chief Economist of New Century Advisors Claudia Sahm supported the hold but pointed out that the May Personal Consumption Expenditures (PCE) inflation is projected to print at or slightly above 4%—double the Fed’s 2% target.
      • Supply Shocks: Sahm noted that the current inflation uptick is driven by overlapping supply shocks (such as energy and tariffs). Textbook monetary policy suggests "looking through" these temporary shocks rather than raising rates and causing undue economic pain.
  • A Rapid Hawkish Shift: Host Mark Zandi highlighted a dramatic swing in the Fed’s bias over a six-week period, moving from an easing bias to a tightening bias in the latest dot plot.
      • Labor Market Concerns: Zandi expressed skepticism about the durability of the labor market, citing declining participation rates despite recent positive job growth. He warned that the Fed risks over-tightening into a softening economy.
      • Rate Hike Risks: Sahm noted that if energy shocks persist and inflation does not make notable progress by autumn, the case for rate hikes will grow, even if it comes at a high cost to wage growth and employment.

The Battle Over Transparency and the "Dot Plot"

  • Minimalist Communication Style: The FOMC statement was stripped of almost all forward-looking guidance, offering no explanation of the Fed's reaction function or the economic variables they are tracking.
  • The Dot Plot on Life Support: Chair Warsh did not participate in the dot plot of the Summary of Economic Projections (SEP). Warsh has historically argued that writing down a policy plan boxes the Fed in.
      • The Case for Transparency: Zandi strongly criticized this shift, arguing that a return to a "Greenspan-esque" opaque era will increase market volatility, force investors to guess the Fed's moves, and open the door to crony capitalism.
      • The Case Against the Dot Plot: Co-host Chris deRitis pushed back, arguing that the anonymous dot plot introduces artificial market volatility because investors treat it as a firm commitment. DeRitis favors either making the dots non-anonymous or removing them entirely while keeping the broader SEP.
  • The "Shadow" Fed Chair Risk: Sahm warned that if the Fed Chair refuses to communicate detailed economic thinking, markets will look elsewhere. Investors will simply designate a "shadow" Fed Chair by focusing on speeches from other vocal governors like Chris Waller or Lisa Cook.

Warsh's Proposed Structural Reforms

  • Balance Sheet Reductions: Warsh has established task forces to re-evaluate the Fed's large balance sheet and its "ample reserves" framework, which he has long opposed.
      • Panel Skepticism: Sahm and deRitis expressed deep skepticism, viewing balance sheet reduction as a massive drain of time and energy that does not solve a pressing economic problem.
      • Debt Monetization Concerns: DeRitis noted that critics view the Fed's massive Treasury holdings as monetizing the national debt and artificially depressing interest rates, which encourages profligate government spending.
  • Rethinking Inflation Metrics: Warsh is advocating for the use of alternative inflation measures, such as the trimmed mean CPI/PCE, rather than relying solely on the PCE deflator.
      • The Trimmed Mean Dilemma: Sahm noted that while the Dallas Fed's trimmed mean PCE historically predicts inflation well, it can fail during unique supply shocks, as it did when it missed the initial inflation surge in 2021.
      • Undermining Data Agencies: Sahm expressed concern over Warsh's harsh rhetoric regarding U.S. statistical agencies, whom he referred to as "echoes of history," warning against attacking the "referee" that creates the data.

***

Notable Quotes

"Show your work. Make sure the American people know that these people entrusted with this decision are thinking, talking about it, and grappling with the issue... If you promise price stability, tell us nothing about how you're going to accomplish it, and it doesn't happen, people are going to be really unhappy."

— *Claudia Sahm*

"In my mind, it’s hard to be too transparent. If you don't provide that information, people are just going to be guessing and flailing, and there's going to be a lot more volatility in markets. Of all the things Warsh has suggested, his shift to opaqueness is the one thing he can change unilaterally, and it's the one I'm most nervous about."

— *Mark Zandi*

"The risk of providing too much guidance is that you could either be wrong and cause market volatility, or even worse, you become biased to stick to your own guidance rather than maintaining the flexibility to move with the data."

— *Chris deRitis*

AWS Summit New York City 2026 - Keynote | Amazon Web Services

Amazon Web Services(841.0K)·73:35·69.6K views·2026-06-22
Matt GarmanCEO, Amazon Web Services
TL;DRAt the AWS Summit NYC 2026, AWS announced a massive expansion of its agentic AI ecosystem, introducing unified context and autonomous tools across workspace productivity (Amazon Quick), enterprise security (AWS Continuum), continuous software delivery (Kiro, DevOps Agent, and Transform), and custom agent infrastructure (Amazon Bedrock AgentCore).

TL;DR

At the AWS Summit NYC 2026, AWS announced a massive expansion of its agentic AI ecosystem, introducing unified context and autonomous tools across workspace productivity (Amazon Quick), enterprise security (AWS Continuum), continuous software delivery (Kiro, DevOps Agent, and Transform), and custom agent infrastructure (Amazon Bedrock AgentCore). These tools aim to eliminate human orchestration bottlenecks, allowing organizations to build compounding operational momentum.

1. Redefining Workplace Productivity with Amazon Quick

  • The Fragmentation Bottleneck: Traditional AI assistants operate in walled gardens, functioning as isolated search tools with short-term memory that force humans to act as the manual "orchestration layer" to copy and paste data across silos (e.g., Slack, OneDrive, Google Drive).
  • Amazon Quick & The Knowledge Graph: Amazon Quick uses an agentic search layer called the *Knowledge Graph* to reason across an organization's entire data estate—mapping relationships between people, documents, communications, and data lakes. It dynamically learns and compounds context with every query.
  • Key Visual and Autonomic Features:
      • Direct Data Queries: Users can query complex structured databases using natural language. Quick automatically drafts SQL queries, samples schemas, and builds interactive visualizations using the QuickSight platform.
      • Activity Feed & Proactive Highlights: Features a personalized activity feed that learns project relevance and user preferences over time.
      • Persistence Agents: Allows non-technical users to build scheduled agents (such as a *Marketing Performance Agent*) that autonomously monitor and update reports 24/7.
  • Proven Enterprise Outcomes:
      • GoDaddy: Eliminated 15,000 hours of manual work annually.
      • Aderant: Achieved 90% faster business insights and a 75% improvement in documentation accuracy.
      • NBA: Structured over 25 years of player prospect data into interactive, real-time leaderboards and benchmarks.

2. Bridging Speed and Safety with AWS Continuum

  • The Paradigm Shift: Security operations are moving from a reactive model of "telemetry, storage, query, and dashboards for humans" to an active model of "context, reasoning, and actions for agents."
  • Introducing AWS Continuum: A comprehensive security agent suite designed to eliminate the historical friction between rapid software deployment and organizational risk.
      • Threat Modeling: Automatically generates threat models directly from raw code, mapping them to system architecture, source code, and design documents to mitigate risks across all six STRIDE categories.
      • Penetration Testing: SmugMug utilized Continuum to run full, context-aware penetration tests on demand, compressing a process that typically took weeks down to hours.
  • Code Vulnerabilities Capability (Preview): Developed alongside design partners like Capital One, MongoDB, Rivian, and Robinhood, this model-agnostic feature operates across four core stages:
      • *Discovery:* Scans backlogs and active cloud environments to build a comprehensive map of vulnerabilities and attack paths.
      • *Prioritization:* Evaluates and contextually ranks threats by reasoning across AWS infrastructure, permissions, network topology, and unstructured business risk data.
      • *Validation:* To minimize false positives, the agent builds and executes reproducible test cases inside a sandbox environment, producing human-reviewable evidence.
      • *Remediation:* Determines and validates precise code fixes or blocking controls. Security teams can run the tool in a supervised "lone mode" before graduating it to automated "enforce mode."

3. The Continuous Software Delivery Loop: Kiro, DevOps Agent, and Transform

  • The Software Delivery Loop: To stop buggy, machine-generated code from creating compounding technical debt, AWS introduced a unified, continuous loop: *write it right, ship it fast, and keep it modern*.
  • Kiro (Write It Right): Kiro is an engineering agent that drafts clear requirements, structured design documents, and validated tests *before* writing any code.
      • Fintech Case Study (Dhan): Using Kiro, a single engineer built a highly complex charting platform featuring 170+ indicators in just 8 weeks—a project estimated to take 12 engineers up to 24 months.
      • Kiro Mobile App (iOS): Developers can kick off spec-driven coding workflows, review pull requests, and approve deployments from their mobile phones. The sessions run securely in the cloud and sync context instantly with the developer's laptop.
  • AWS DevOps Agent (Ship It Fast):
      • Release Management (Preview): Moves the DevOps Agent from a reactive SRE tool to a proactive release pipeline. It validates builds, runs production risk assessments, and conducts autonomous testing in sandboxes to catch regressions before they impact users.
  • AWS Transform (Keep It Modern):
      • Continuous Modernization (Preview): While previous versions of Transform required manual activation, this new continuous background agent automatically crawls repositories to upgrade frameworks, update dependencies, and resolve version compliance issues.
      • Enterprise Adoption: Southwest Airlines scaled Kiro to 2,700 developers (two-thirds of its engineering organization), utilizing the tool to accelerate legacy codebase modernization and pull its platform modernization timeline in by three years.

4. Scaling Custom Agents with Bedrock AgentCore and AWS Context

  • Amazon Bedrock AgentCore Harness (GA): Building custom agent infrastructure (session memory, error recovery, orchestration, and API tool access) typically takes months. AgentCore Harness decouples this infrastructure from the model, allowing developers to spin up secure, isolated microVM agents with just three API calls.
  • AgentCore Policies: Deterministic guardrails enforced *outside* the agent's code, preventing bad actors from manipulating models or bypassing security parameters via prompt injection. It will soon integrate signals from major security providers like CrowdStrike, Netskope, SentinelOne, and Zscaler.
  • The Unified Context Layer:
      • Web Search: grounds responses in real-time, public web information. This managed tool operates entirely within the AWS secure boundary.
      • Managed Knowledge Base: Integrates unstructured organizational data (S3, SharePoint, Google Drive, Confluence) using an "agentic retriever" to answer multi-step questions. (Currently used by OpenAI to power its large-scale RAG pipelines).
      • AWS Context (New Service): Automatically infers relationships across structured databases (stored as S3 Iceberg tables) and unstructured files to build an enterprise-wide knowledge graph. This service applies semantic reasoning (e.g., understanding that "escalations" and "tickets" refer to the same concept) to serve custom agents with highly accurate business context.
  • Infrastructure Demands: Swami Sivasubramanian highlighted that multiple agentic reasoning steps require massive scale. In Q1 2026, Amazon Bedrock processed more requests than in all previous years combined. GPT-4o and GPT-4o-mini are now fully integrated on the platform.

Notable Quotes

"Agents, when they are built correctly, get better the more you use them. More interactions mean more context. And more context means better outcomes... This is a virtuous cycle. And that is compounding momentum." — Dr. Swami Sivasubramanian, Vice President, Agentic AI, AWS
"Telemetry without context is noise. But telemetry with context is signal. And when you have signal and you can reason through it, you have actionable insights that can be taken." — Chet Kapoor, VP, Search, Security, and Observability, AWS
"Don't let your infrastructure be the ceiling on your ambition. The tools exist today to move faster and run in parallel, and to turn complexity into advantage." — Lauren, Southwest Airlines Tech Representative

The PGA TOUR is writing tournament coverage agents 10x faster, Epsilon increased productivity by 3 to 5x, and Nasdaq, Thomson Reuters, Visa, and Experian are scaling agents throughout their enterprises. But what is it that enables the PGA agent to write sports coverage? You might think it's about using different models for different use cases. But it's actually using a different harness. Think of the model as the agent's brain and the harness as the body. The harness provides everything that the brain needs to actually get the work done: state persistence, error recovery, context management, and session isolation. The harness has as much influence on an agent's output as the model. But creating an agent harness can take months of engineering before your customers see a single sign of intelligence. We wanted to give you that time back. That's why we are excited to launch the general availability of the AgentCore harness. We have removed the bottleneck of harness development so you can go from idea to production in just minutes. You declare what you want your agent to do, the model it uses, the tool it calls, and the instructions it follows. And AgentCore handles the rest. Just three API calls to get an agent up and running. Under the hood, AgentCore does the hard work for you. It assembles the orchestration loop, tool execution, memory management, and error recovery and so forth. Your agent runs in an isolated microVM without you needing to provision anything. With AgentCore, the harness is decoupled from the model, so you can easily change models without having to change your harness. And when you need more control, like custom orchestration logic where you want to actually do your own routing, you can easily export your harness into Strands-based logic code. And then you can start coding with your favorite agentic coding tool, and then you're good to go. Now, talking about Strands, as many of you will remember, Strands is the open-source toolkit that we launched last year, and it provides complete control over how people can build their agent harness. Strands Harness helps you build a custom harness, while Strands Shell, which we just launched yesterday, gives your agent sandbox file and code access that launches in under a millisecond with no container setup required. And Strands Evals lets you inject real tool failures and adversarial attacks at build time, so that you find where things break before your customers do. We open-sourced Strands in May of last year, and since then, it has been downloaded over 50 million times. A great harness makes your agent capable, but capable agents also introduce new risks. The brain of every agent is a model, and models can't reliably distinguish between instructions and data. That means a bad actor can embed instructions into a file your agent reads and start steering it in a way you did not intend. Protections inside the agent's code won't always help, because if the model can read those protections, it can also be manipulated into ignoring them. You need controls that sit outside the agent's code, that control the model so that it can't reason around them. This is why we built AgentCore policies: deterministic controls that define what your agent can do and cannot do. All enforcement happens outside the agent's code, where the agent can't bypass it. And now, AgentCore gives you the ability to evaluate agent actions and their response to prompt attacks, harmful content, and sensitive data using policy guardrails. Coming soon, you will be able to integrate signals from leading security providers, including Check Point, Netskope, Rubrik, SentinelOne, and Zscaler, into those same AgentCore policies. Guardrails define what your agent is and is not allowed to do. But making sure that they make the right call for your business takes one more thing: context. Context is what makes your agent's tenth decision better than its first. And that's what separates agents that compound from agents that just simply go faster. But even the smartest model has no idea how your business actually works. It doesn't know your customers, or your systems, or your data. An agent that doesn't pause when it doesn't know the answer will confidently give you the wrong answer. The right answer requires the right context. And context lives in your data. When we talk about data, I classify them into three kinds. There is public data, like what's happening right now in markets, in the news, and on social. And then, your company's unstructured knowledge—think of documents, images, and videos. And then, you have your company's structured data sitting in data lakes, data warehouses, and databases. Now, let's start with public data. Every model has a knowledge cutoff, a day its picture of the world froze in its pre-training. If you ask a model for a competitive analysis, you need it to know about the product your competitor announced yesterday, not the old information from the model's training data. That information lives on the web. Inside Amazon, we have been combining various knowledge with web intelligence to answer complex questions for a while now across these three products. And customers kept asking us the same question: "Why can't we have the same level of web intelligence for our agents so that they can do that?" I'm happy to share that the same battle-tested agentic web search that powers Quick, KIRO, and Alexa Plus is now available for all your agents. Connect it, and your agent can ground its response in current, real-time, accurate web information, no integration work required. Web search is a fully managed tool on AgentCore and coming soon to Amazon Bedrock. It returns re-ranked current web results and operates natively within your environment, so your data and queries never leave AWS. Whether you're building a deep research agent to do various investigation reports that cross-reference public sources, or you're building a travel assistant that compares different sites and listings, your agent can now reason over the web. Now, let's talk about your company's unstructured data. Ten years of documents, PDFs, images, and videos. They are scattered across SharePoint, Confluence, Google Drive, and S3. The answer your agent needs exists in this data, and it's probably just buried in 15 different places in 12 different formats. Connecting, parsing, and retrieving all of them accurately is a massive lift. That's why yesterday, we announced Bedrock Managed Knowledge Base, helping you ground agent responses in your latest organizational data with just a few clicks. Managed Knowledge Base provides native connectors to data sources like S3, SharePoint, Confluence, and Google Drive, and AWS handles all the other parts: the ingestion, parsing, storage, and retrieval. It provides built-in access control that enforces document-level permissions, so users only receive responses from the content they are authorized to access. You can use Managed Knowledge Base as a tool in AgentCore, and all knowledge bases that you create here are ready to be consumed by Amazon Quick by default. And for complex, multi-step questions, we built something smarter here: an agentic retriever. It plans queries across your knowledge base, connects various concepts across documents, evaluates what it finds, and re-ranks them so your agent delivers the best answer, not just the closest vector match. Thousands of customers are already building on managed knowledge bases, including OpenAI, who are using its RAG capabilities to ground the inference calls and model responses reliably at scale for millions of users with the right customer context. Now, the final tranche of your context stays inside data warehouses, data lakes, and databases. This structured data presents a unique retrieval challenge. To make intelligent querying of structured data possible, agents need to understand the syntax or the semantics of your data: what tables exist, what the columns really mean, how they relate to each other, and what sources are authoritative for which data. In fact, you saw earlier, when Brian demoed it, how Amazon Quick is solving this through a semantic knowledge store that we call N-Store. Hundreds of thousands of users within Amazon have been interacting daily with Quick's production knowledge graph. When an agent needs to answer a question, the knowledge store tells Quick which data they need to use, how those sources relate to each other, and what business rules they should apply. It combines semantic search with graph-level reasoning. So if a user asks about escalations and the dashboard calls them tickets, it knows those two mean exactly the same thing. Every day, the semantic knowledge store processes over 1.8 million requests for Quick. But businesses don't think of their data in terms of structured and unstructured. You want unified context across all your data, regardless of where it lives or what it takes. You already saw the possibilities unlocked by unified context with Amazon Quick. We have also been working with customers who are building this context layer between their raw data and their agents. The common challenge happens to be that building these graphs is still bespoke, with no standard service to automate and maintain them constantly. And today, I'm excited to announce AWS Context. This service automatically builds a knowledge graph from all your existing data. It infers relationships across your data assets, business rules, and domain knowledge, making all of it available to your agents and your organization at runtime. There is no infrastructure to provision and no retrieval pipeline to build. And with just a few clicks in the management console, your agents now have governed context. With AWS Context, your agents get smarter without you having to rebuild anything from scratch. The knowledge graph improves itself over time as it learns which sources produce correct results and which parts get used, with all the metadata from your structured and unstructured data sources stored in Iceberg format in S3 tables. You can build against it with the tools you already use, with no proprietary APIs. And you can define how agents use your data by attaching instructions or skills to your data assets. Agent skills are governed, versioned, and updated in one place. Agents on AgentCore inherit them automatically. In production, your agents query the graph through agentic search APIs and NCP tools. They can find the right data and apply the right business rules faster and more accurately than manually maintained context allows. Your data team can review these inferred relationships, edit them, promote them to production, and attach domain knowledge directly through the console. So now we have given you the foundation to build agents, the guardrails to keep them safe, and the context to make them compound. But there is one more aspect to creating great agents, and that is the models and infrastructure. Because every time an agent reasons, plans, and checks or corrects its work, that's an inference call. In fact, a single agent interaction isn't one call; it might be 10, 20, or even 50. Multiply those 50 calls by billions of agents, and inferences are on track to become the biggest workload on the planet. This means how you run inference is no longer an infrastructure detail; it becomes part of your business strategy. That's why we built Amazon Bedrock, and why we never stop improving it. It enables you to get the best performance, reliability, and security when you use your models at scale for your most critical and demanding business applications. And you are already voting for it with your workloads. In Q1 of this year alone, Bedrock processed more requests than all the previous years combined. We continue to make Amazon Bedrock a great place for all types of models, so you can pick the right ones for your agents, and that includes OpenAI's GPT-4o and 4o-mini, which are now available. And to help you get the most out of these models, we recently added capabilities like advanced prompt optimization, which helps you migrate from one model generation to the next, so that you can improve and automatically compare results across up to five models with built-in and custom evaluations. We also delivered granular cost attribution by user, by team, and by application, flowing right into the AWS Cost Explorer. And we have built production-grade observability through CloudWatch, providing per-model latency, error breakdowns, and throughput trends. So we started today with a very simple idea: using AI the right way should create momentum that constantly compounds. And compounding momentum is now your most valuable asset. Today, we showed you how you are using your momentum that never stops: agents for working (Quick delivers outcomes); agents for securing (Continuum finds, prioritizes, and remediates at machine speed); agents for building (KIRO writes it right, Release Agent ships it fast, and Transform keeps it modern); and agents you create (AgentCore context and Bedrock underneath all of it). At AWS, our job is to remove every bottleneck between your imagination and what you can build.
